(Mainichi/Takehiko Onishi)\\n\\nOSAKA -- As a completely blind person, this Mainichi Shimbun reporter was alarmed and felt at a loss atop the \\"Grand Ring,\\" the large structure bounding the Expo 2025 Osaka, Kansai venue, when the tactile guideway blocks I had been relying on suddenly ended.\\n\\nI had been following the raised linear braille blocks, which indicate the direction to go, along about a 2-kilmeter circular walkway. Eventually, I reached a point where these guiding tiles ceased unexpectedly.\\n\\nThe walkway, about 12 meters above ground, split into two, one branch a slope going up to the highest level, some 20 meters high. At the fork, a series of dotted tactile warning tiles -- meant to alert pedestrians to use caution -- span the pathway, but no directional guide tiles follow beyond this point. I was unaware of this until informed by a sighted reporter who accompanied me.\\n\\nThe circular shape of the rooftop walkway itself creates a barrier for blind visitors like myself, making it impossible to know one's precise location within the endless loop. I found no braille signage on the corridor's handrails, nor any audible guidance.\\n\\nJapan invented tactile paving in the 1960s as an innovative tool enhancing navigation and safety for visually impaired people. The Expo's ring structure, billed as one of the largest wooden buildings in the world, is meant to represent a message of \\"unity in diversity.\\" With the Expo having opened on April 13, the venue should truly become an inclusive space where everyone can equally enjoy themselves, whether they have disabilities or not. (Mainichi/Takehiko Onishi)\n\nOSAKA -- As a completely blind person, this Mainichi Shimbun reporter was alarmed and felt at a loss atop the \"Grand Ring,\" the large structure bounding the Expo 2025 Osaka, Kansai venue, when the tactile guideway blocks I had been relying on suddenly ended.\n\nI had been following the raised linear braille blocks, which indicate the direction to go, along about a 2-kilmeter circular walkway. Eventually, I reached a point where these guiding tiles ceased unexpectedly.\n\nThe walkway, about 12 meters above ground, split into two, one branch a slope going up to the highest level, some 20 meters high. At the fork, a series of dotted tactile warning tiles -- meant to alert pedestrians to use caution -- span the pathway, but no directional guide tiles follow beyond this point. I was unaware of this until informed by a sighted reporter who accompanied me.\n\nThe circular shape of the rooftop walkway itself creates a barrier for blind visitors like myself, making it impossible to know one's precise location within the endless loop. I found no braille signage on the corridor's handrails, nor any audible guidance.\n\nJapan invented tactile paving in the 1960s as an innovative tool enhancing navigation and safety for visually impaired people. The Expo's ring structure, billed as one of the largest wooden buildings in the world, is meant to represent a message of \"unity in diversity.\" With the Expo having opened on April 13, the venue should truly become an inclusive space where everyone can equally enjoy themselves, whether they have disabilities or not. It appears organizers still lack that last crucial step of imagination necessary to achieve genuine accessibility.\n\n(Japanese original by Ayato Saki, Braille Mainichi Department)\n\n- [Font Size](https://mainichi.jp/mainichi.jp)\n - S\n - M\n - L\n- [Print](javascript:void(0);)\n\n## Related Articles\n\n- [What led Expo 2005 Aichi to achieve its visitor target despite initial low attendance?](https://mainichi.jp/english/articles/20250418/p2a/00m/0na/029000c)\n\n## Also in The Mainichi\n\nThe Mainichi on social media\n\n- [RSS](https://mainichi.jp/english/rss/)\n\n## Latest Articles\n\n- [![Kunishige Kamamoto (Kyodo) ](https://cdn.mainichi.jp/vol1/2025/08/10/20250810p2g00m0sp031000p/6.jpg?1)\\\nFootball: Japan national team's record scorer Kamamoto dies at 81](https://mainichi.jp/english/articles/20250810/p2g/00m/0sp/032000c)\n- [![Russian President Vladimir Pu",

      "id": "https://asia.nikkei.com/Spotlight/Datawatch/Japan-Inc.-shows-signs-of-faster-rejuvenation",
      "title": "Japan Inc. shows signs of faster rejuvenation",
      "url": "https://asia.nikkei.com/Spotlight/Datawatch/Japan-Inc.-shows-signs-of-faster-rejuvenation",
      "publishedDate": "2024-07-06T00:00:00.000Z",
      "author": "Staff Writer",
      "text": "TOKYO -- At long last, Japan Inc. is showing signs of faster transformation, with both corporate births and closures on the rise. In 2023, over 140,000 companies were established, an increase of nearly 10% from the previous year. Closures also rose, partly due to the phaseout of COVID-19 pandemic support for smaller businesses. With wages, interest rates and inflation all rising, price mechanisms and other market disciplines are beginning to drive swift adaptation among businesses. These developments may finally signal an end to Japan's prolonged period of low economic growth. \"Starting a business was easy, as there was a lot of support available,\" said Shoken Nakase, the CEO of Recept, a developer of online verification apps, which have been in increasing demand since online transactions surged amid the pandemic. The former engineer founded the company in October. An analysis of data from the National Tax Agency reveals that corporate registrations began to notably increase in 2021, surging to 142,659 in 2023. This was an 8.9% rise from the previous year and the highest since comparable data became available in 2016. Both a post-pandemic recovery and increased government support have contributed to the rise in newly founded businesses. In 2022, the government unveiled a policy aimed at creating 100,000 startups. Starting in fiscal 2023, it expanded tax breaks to encourage investment in emerging companies. Additionally, in fiscal 2024, the state-run Japan Finance Corp. raised the cap on unsecured, unguaranteed loans for launching new businesses. \n \n \n \n The increase in business creation has also been supported by advancements in digitalization. \"It seems that hurdles to starting businesses in rural areas have significantly decreased due to the widespread use of online meetings and other technological advancements,\" said Iichiro Uesugi, a professor at Hitotsubashi University. New businesses can also benefit from new social security plans. On June 1, a group of startups established the nation's first health insurance association for workers at younger companies. It offers lower premiums than traditional health insurance plans for small and midsize businesses, easing the financial burdens for both individual participants and member companies. The number of companies that exit the market is also on the rise, another sign that Japan's corporate metabolism is accelerating. Last year, 43,187 businesses were deregistered, a 14.5% increase from the previous year. The number of bankruptcies, which had dropped below 6,000 in fiscal 2021 for the first time in 57 years, surpassed 9,000 in fiscal 2023 as repayments began in earnest on zero-interest unsecured loans that had been extended during the pandemic crisis. \"Despite government support, I saw no prospects of earnings recovery,\" said a man who once ran more than 10 restaurants in Tokyo and other locations. Bankruptcy proceedings for his company began in the spring of 2023. The business environment is beco"

\"https://asia.nikkei.com/Spotlight/Datawatch/Japan-Inc.-shows-signs-of-faster-rejuvenation\",\n      \"publishedDate\": \"2024-07-06T00:00:00.000Z\",\n      \"author\": \"Staff Writer\",\n      \"text\": \"TOKYO -- At long last, Japan Inc. is showing signs of faster transformation, with both corporate births and closures on the rise. In 2023, over 140,000 companies were established, an increase of nearly 10% from the previous year. Closures also rose, partly due to the phaseout of COVID-19 pandemic support for smaller businesses. With wages, interest rates and inflation all rising, price mechanisms and other market disciplines are beginning to drive swift adaptation among businesses. These developments may finally signal an end to Japan's prolonged period of low economic growth. \\"Starting a business was easy, as there was a lot of support available,\\" said Shoken Nakase, the CEO of Recept, a developer of online verification apps, which have been in increasing demand since online transactions surged amid the pandemic. The former engineer founded the company in October. An analysis of data from the National Tax Agency reveals that corporate registrations began to notably increase in 2021, surging to 142,659 in 2023. This was an 8.9% rise from the previous year and the highest since comparable data became available in 2016. Both a post-pandemic recovery and increased government support have contributed to the rise in newly founded businesses. In 2022, the government unveiled a policy aimed at creating 100,000 startups. Starting in fiscal 2023, it expanded tax breaks to encourage investment in emerging companies. Additionally, in fiscal 2024, the state-run Japan Finance Corp. raised the cap on unsecured, unguaranteed loans for launching new businesses. \n \n \n \n The increase in business creation has also been supported by advancements in digitalization. \\"It seems that hurdles to starting businesses in rural areas have significantly decreased due to the widespread use of online meetings and other technological advancements,\\" said Iichiro Uesugi, a professor at Hitotsubashi University. New businesses can also benefit from new social security plans. On June 1, a group of startups established the nation's first health insurance association for workers at younger companies. It offers lower premiums than traditional health insurance plans for small and midsize businesses, easing the financial burdens for both individual participants and member companies. The number of companies that exit the market is also on the rise, another sign that Japan's corporate metabolism is accelerating. Last year, 43,187 businesses were deregistered, a 14.5% increase from the previous year. The number of bankruptcies, which had dropped below 6,000 in fiscal 2021 for the first time in 57 years, surpassed 9,000 in fiscal 2023 as repayments began in earnest on zero-interest unsecured loans that had been extended during the pandemic crisis. \\"Despite government support, I saw no prospects of earnings recovery,\\" said a man who once ran more than 10 restaurants in Tokyo and other locations. Bankruptcy proceedings for his company began in the spring of 2023. \"https://asia.nikkei.com/Spotlight/Datawatch/Japan-Inc.-shows-signs-of-faster-rejuvenation\",\n      \"publishedDate\": \"2024-07-06T00:00:00.000Z\",\n      \"author\": \"Staff Writer\",\n      \"text\": \"TOKYO -- At long last, Japan Inc. is showing signs of faster transformation, with both corporate births and closures on the rise. In 2023, over 140,000 companies were established, an increase of nearly 10% from the previous year. Closures also rose, partly due to the phaseout of COVID-19 pandemic support for smaller businesses. With wages, interest rates and inflation all rising, price mechanisms and other market disciplines are beginning to drive swift adaptation among businesses. These developments may finally signal an end to Japan's prolonged period of low economic growth. \\"Starting a business was easy, as there was a lot of support available,\\" said Shoken Nakase, the CEO of Recept, a developer of online verification apps, which have been in increasing demand since online transactions surged amid the pandemic. The former engineer founded the company in October. An analysis of data from the National Tax Agency reveals that corporate registrations began to notably increase in 2021, surging to 142,659 in 2023. This was an 8.9% rise from the previous year and the highest since comparable data became available in 2016. Both a post-pandemic recovery and increased government support have contributed to the rise in newly founded businesses. In 2022, the government unveiled a policy aimed at creating 100,000 startups. Starting in fiscal 2023, it expanded tax breaks to encourage investment in emerging companies. Additionally, in fiscal 2024, the state-run Japan Finance Corp. raised the cap on unsecured, unguaranteed loans for launching new businesses. \n \n \n \n The increase in business creation has also been supported by advancements in digitalization. \\"It seems that hurdles to starting businesses in rural areas have significantly decreased due to the widespread use of online meetings and other technological advancements,\\" said Iichiro Uesugi, a professor at Hitotsubashi University. New businesses can also benefit from new social security plans. On June 1, a group of startups established the nation's first health insurance association for workers at younger companies. It offers lower premiums than traditional health insurance plans for small and midsize businesses, easing the financial burdens for both individual participants and member companies. The number of companies that exit the market is also on the rise, another sign that Japan's corporate metabolism is accelerating. Last year, 43,187 businesses were deregistered, a 14.5% increase from the previous year. The number of bankruptcies, which had dropped below 6,000 in fiscal 2021 for the first time in 57 years, surpassed 9,000 in fiscal 2023 as repayments began in earnest on zero-interest unsecured loans that had been extended during the pandemic crisis. \\"Despite government support, I saw no prospects of earnings recovery,\\" said a man who once ran more than 10 restaurants in Tokyo and other locations. Bankruptcy proceedings for his company began in the spring of 2023. It offers lower premiums than traditional health insurance plans for small and midsize businesses, easing the financial burdens for both individual participants and member companies. \"https://asia.nikkei.com/Spotlight/Datawatch/Japan-Inc.-shows-signs-of-faster-rejuvenation\",\n      \"publishedDate\": \"2024-07-06T00:00:00.000Z\",\n      \"author\": \"Staff Writer\",\n      \"text\": \"TOKYO -- At long last, Japan Inc. is showing signs of faster transformation, with both corporate births and closures on the rise. In 2023, over 140,000 companies were established, an increase of nearly 10% from the previous year. Closures also rose, partly due to the phaseout of COVID-19 pandemic support for smaller businesses. With wages, interest rates and inflation all rising, price mechanisms and other market disciplines are beginning to drive swift adaptation among businesses. These developments may finally signal an end to Japan's prolonged period of low economic growth. \\"Starting a business was easy, as there was a lot of support available,\\" said Shoken Nakase, the CEO of Recept, a developer of online verification apps, which have been in increasing demand since online transactions surged amid the pandemic. The former engineer founded the company in October. An analysis of data from the National Tax Agency reveals that corporate registrations began to notably increase in 2021, surging to 142,659 in 2023. This was an 8.9% rise from the previous year and the highest since comparable data became available in 2016. Both a post-pandemic recovery and increased government support have contributed to the rise in newly founded businesses. In 2022, the government unveiled a policy aimed at creating 100,000 startups. Starting in fiscal 2023, it expanded tax breaks to encourage investment in emerging companies. Additionally, in fiscal 2024, the state-run Japan Finance Corp. raised the cap on unsecured, unguaranteed loans for launching new businesses. \n \n \n \n The increase in business creation has also been supported by advancements in digitalization. \\"It seems that hurdles to starting businesses in rural areas have significantly decreased due to the widespread use of online meetings and other technological advancements,\\" said Iichiro Uesugi, a professor at Hitotsubashi University. New businesses can also benefit from new social security plans. On June 1, a group of startups established the nation's first health insurance association for workers at younger companies. It offers lower premiums than traditional health insurance plans for small and midsize businesses, easing the financial burdens for both individual participants and member companies. The number of companies that exit the market is also on the rise, another sign that Japan's corporate metabolism is accelerating. Last year, 43,187 businesses were deregistered, a 14.5% increase from the previous year. The number of bankruptcies, which had dropped below 6,000 in fiscal 2021 for the first time in 57 years, surpassed 9,000 in fiscal 2023 as repayments began in earnest on zero-interest unsecured loans that had been extended during the pandemic crisis. \\"Despite government support, I saw no prospects of earnings recovery,\\" said a man who once ran more than 10 restaurants in Tokyo and other locations. Bankruptcy proceedings for his company began in the spring of 2023. \"text\": \"TOKYO -- At long last, Japan Inc. is showing signs of faster transformation, with both corporate births and closures on the rise. In 2023, over 140,000 companies were established, an increase of nearly 10% from the previous year. Closures also rose, partly due to the phaseout of COVID-19 pandemic support for smaller businesses. With wages, interest rates and inflation all rising, price mechanisms and other market disciplines are beginning to drive swift adaptation among businesses. These developments may finally signal an end to Japan's prolonged period of low economic growth. \\"Starting a business was easy, as there was a lot of support available,\\" said Shoken Nakase, the CEO of Recept, a developer of online verification apps, which have been in increasing demand since online transactions surged amid the pandemic. The former engineer founded the company in October. An analysis of data from the National Tax Agency reveals that corporate registrations began to notably increase in 2021, surging to 142,659 in 2023. This was an 8.9% rise from the previous year and the highest since comparable data became available in 2016. Both a post-pandemic recovery and increased government support have contributed to the rise in newly founded businesses. In 2022, the government unveiled a policy aimed at creating 100,000 startups. Starting in fiscal 2023, it expanded tax breaks to encourage investment in emerging companies. Additionally, in fiscal 2024, the state-run Japan Finance Corp. raised the cap on unsecured, unguaranteed loans for launching new businesses. \n \n \n \n The increase in business creation has also been supported by advancements in digitalization. \\"It seems that hurdles to starting businesses in rural areas have significantly decreased due to the widespread use of online meetings and other technological advancements,\\" said Iichiro Uesugi, a professor at Hitotsubashi University. New businesses can also benefit from new social security plans. On June 1, a group of startups established the nation's first health insurance association for workers at younger companies. It offers lower premiums than traditional health insurance plans for small and midsize businesses, easing the financial burdens for both individual participants and member companies. The number of companies that exit the market is also on the rise, another sign that Japan's corporate metabolism is accelerating. Last year, 43,187 businesses were deregistered, a 14.5% increase from the previous year. The number of bankruptcies, which had dropped below 6,000 in fiscal 2021 for the first time in 57 years, surpassed 9,000 in fiscal 2023 as repayments began in earnest on zero-interest unsecured loans that had been extended during the pandemic crisis. \\"Despite government support, I saw no prospects of earnings recovery,\\" said a man who once ran more than 10 restaurants in Tokyo and other locations. \"text\": \"TOKYO -- At long last, Japan Inc. is showing signs of faster transformation, with both corporate births and closures on the rise. In 2023, over 140,000 companies were established, an increase of nearly 10% from the previous year. Closures also rose, partly due to the phaseout of COVID-19 pandemic support for smaller businesses. With wages, interest rates and inflation all rising, price mechanisms and other market disciplines are beginning to drive swift adaptation among businesses. These developments may finally signal an end to Japan's prolonged period of low economic growth. \\"Starting a business was easy, as there was a lot of support available,\\" said Shoken Nakase, the CEO of Recept, a developer of online verification apps, which have been in increasing demand since online transactions surged amid the pandemic. The former engineer founded the company in October. An analysis of data from the National Tax Agency reveals that corporate registrations began to notably increase in 2021, surging to 142,659 in 2023. This was an 8.9% rise from the previous year and the highest since comparable data became available in 2016. Both a post-pandemic recovery and increased government support have contributed to the rise in newly founded businesses. In 2022, the government unveiled a policy aimed at creating 100,000 startups. Starting in fiscal 2023, it expanded tax breaks to encourage investment in emerging companies. Additionally, in fiscal 2024, the state-run Japan Finance Corp. raised the cap on unsecured, unguaranteed loans for launching new businesses. \n \n \n \n The increase in business creation has also been supported by advancements in digitalization. \\"It seems that hurdles to starting businesses in rural areas have significantly decreased due to the widespread use of online meetings and other technological advancements,\\" said Iichiro Uesugi, a professor at Hitotsubashi University. New businesses can also benefit from new social security plans. On June 1, a group of startups established the nation's first health insurance association for workers at younger companies. It offers lower premiums than traditional health insurance plans for small and midsize businesses, easing the financial burdens for both individual participants and member companies. The number of companies that exit the market is also on the rise, another sign that Japan's corporate metabolism is accelerating. Last year, 43,187 businesses were deregistered, a 14.5% increase from the previous year. The number of bankruptcies, which had dropped below 6,000 in fiscal 2021 for the first time in 57 years, surpassed 9,000 in fiscal 2023 as repayments began in earnest on zero-interest unsecured loans that had been extended during the pandemic crisis. \\"Despite government support, I saw no prospects of earnings recovery,\\" said a man who once ran more than 10 restaurants in Tokyo and other locations.
